My frustrations with PPM are outlined as follows:

Poor customer service: Often times PPM does not post photos of inside of apartments, are not able to provide basic information about apartments such as square footage. There is not a direct line to speak with the person who is processing your application for questions. They will answer text messages, but generally only one text every 2-3 hours, and will only answer 1 question even if you ask 3. Overall very inefficient processing of applications.

False Advertising: Apartments that were listed as "available now" we found out may not be ready for move in for 2-3 months. Although a site may be listed as available, 7/7 properties that we requested already had approvals for other tenants to live there.

Generally not flexible: Unwilling to accommodate minor changes in rental agreements like month-month leases, unwilling to schedule showings on weekends. Move in dates listed set in stone, not open to negotiation.

Conclusion: I tried long and hard to work with this company to get an apartment as the application was fairly expensive ($84 for a couple) but it turned out to be a huge waste of time and money. As a traveling health care professional, I live in many different apartments nationally and appreciate efficient processing of applications and good communication. If any of these things are priorities for selecting your apartment, save yourself some money and a headache - consider other companies before PPM.</text>

Do not wait for them to 'process' your application. Because PPM, myself and two of my other friends are now homeless. <review>My wife is Japanese, my son is half Japanese and the three of us love sushi. We came here to get our grind on and we were disappointed.

The sushi was good. The restaurant was clean. The parking was safe. The problem was with the people who work there and with how they present their establishment.

The place has a Japanese name. When you enter, you are greeted by enthusiastic shouts of greeting in Japanese. When you leave, you are given words of ‚Äúthanks" in Japanese. Turns out nobody who works here speaks a lick of Japanese beyond those few words.

As we were seated after a short wait, my wife began to chat in a friendly manner to our server, in Japanese. The server said ‚Äúwhat?!‚Äù and looked at her with a look or disgust. The server said flatly, ‚ÄúI don‚Äôt speak Japanese.‚Äù

This Japanese sushi shop is run by Korean Americans who are presenting themselves as Japanese people running a Japanese sushi shop.

After that brief exchange our server was much less than friendly and her conversation with us was kept at a bare minimum for the rest of our meal.

Our sushi chef was a Korean American guy named Jeff. Really.

The only reason this bothered me was because everybody who wasn‚Äôt Japanese were pretending that they were. My Family felt deceived.

In short, the meal was good. Prices were average. The place felt traditional but knowing it is all just a show kind of soured it. Our server developing an attitude for being caught kind of soured it.

<UserId.>112828455244746111861< /UserId.><Name>Alizen< /Name>< Time>

< Rate>
3<//Rate>
< review>
Domo Sushi

If you're hungry and craving sushi in Anaheim Hills but certainly don't want to break your bank, then this is the place for you.

One of the things I like about this restaurant is that it offers BOGO 50% off duplicate rolls, meaning if you order 2 California rolls then one of them would be half off. The quality of the sushi, however, is nothing more than average. Decent portions but nothing about their sushi leaves me wanting more.

It's a very small restaurant in here so it can get pretty packed very easily as they only have seating for about 30 people or so, including the bar. The service wasn't amazing and the waiter hovers over you from a distance which kind of made it very intimidating to order my meal because he was waiting so long nearby.

I love to order miso soup and edamame as an appetizer and while the edamame was perfectly boiled and salted, the miso soup was far too salty in my opinion. I wouldn't immediately cast this restaurant aside as it is a decent place to dine, but at the rate I'm paying I'd rather pay for AYCE sushi.</review>

< review>
I've gotten to know the recover industry well during my off and on struggles in life. The recovery scene in this area is huge. Pacific shores is in a great location, close to the Costa Mesa and Newport Beach Alano clubs, and also close to the free way beach and stores.

The first time I was sober for a good length of time I was happy to do so in this area. I am so grateful to be staying at pacific shores. Honestly, compared to other recovery homes and centers I've visited and stayed at, pacific shores is amazing. It's great to be in an environment where I am surrounded by others who understand what I'm going through and are also pulling their lives back together. Working with addicts and alcoholics is no easy thing to deal with. I can say everyone involved here has the understanding and insight into the baffling and insidious things we can do to ourselves.

While I don't believe you can throw money at every problem, you can absolutely put yourself in an environment that can push you in the direction you need to go in. I'm super glad I'm here. I'm still super afraid to go back. I desperately don't want to feel the way I did before. I'm glad I am here.</review>

I have people to keep me accountable and go to meetings with me.  The other residents and I help each other. <Review>This place has pastries.

Tried both the pumpkin and red bean with mochi pastries. The pumpkin was fresh made, not canned and not like pumpkin pie but like kombucha--a light sweetness.

The red bean with mochi filling was very sweet, in a good way, with a wonderful, glutinous mouthfeel.

Also came for their thick and thin green onion pancakes. Both are good--the thin ones are more about the crispy texture, the thick ones are more about the green onions flavor.

The show stoppers were the pork belly bun and their green leek pastry which was a giant empanada stuffed with green onions, vermicelli, egg, and ground meat. Yum!< /Review>< Pics>

<pictures>None< /pictures><response>None< /response><gmapID>0x80dd4af3cd96f8b9:0xc9175a0074da5903< /gmapID>< Review>
I took the kids for Saturday breakfast.  We used to get soy milk, egg pancake, rice roll in OC from 99 Ranch and this seems to be the only place to get soy milk for breakfast.

We were disappointed in the experience.  The soy milk tasted diluted, both the hot and cold one.  My 5 year old's comment is 'this tastes like water'.

The fried dough inside the rice roll was pretty tough instead of crunchy.  The egg pancake was good, the texture is more doughy than normal.

We came here for dinner awhile back, similar luke warm impression on food.  The restaurant is very cluttered, and as expected of old restaurant, you wondee about cleaniness.

The servers are nice, but when there are more than 3 tables, they seem to get overwhelm and get anxious at each other.<//Review>

Visited this place twice and enjoyed the food both times! So far I've tried the Carne Asada and Al Pastor in Super Burrito form. The burritos are a good portion size and have everything you'd expect from a solid Mexican restaurant. What makes it stand out is how flavorful the meat is; I'd prefer that it were not so finely minced however. I would recommend the Al Pastor as the char on the pork adds nice texture.

Take cash as I believe they charge a small credit card processing fee. Don't let that stop you from some really great food!< /Text>

<Date>1555723410401</Date><Review>My wife and I eat at the food truck in the parking lot.

Really good Mexican food.  The pork is shredded but has a solid flavour.  Would like to highlight that the meat is not watery tasting like other places.  The beef is super cooked but still palatable.  We have tried taccs, super tacos, burritos, and tortas.

The food can be spicy or extra spicy - depending on what you would like.

They also have a restaurant next door that I have eaten at a number of times - similar taste.

It can be busy at times - normally lunch on week days is busy for the restaurant and the truck seems to be quite busy on Saturdays/Sundays around lunch.</Review>< GmapID>
